< Text>
Comfortable vibe, good and seemingly very authentic food, nice owner. Not to be confused with the previous Mongolian restaurant that occupied this location.

Ate:
Khuushuur (meat pastries)
-Very good. A larger portion than I expected. I haven't had this version of the dish before but I've eaten chebureki (the Russian version of the same thing) many times, and this is a good rendition. (To the person who posted the video of draining juice out of the inside of their pastries -- at least if it's like the Russian version, this is exactly how it's supposed to be, rich and juicy inside.)

Buuz
-Like a drier but chewier version of soup dumplings. I've never had a dumpling with meat inside that was this chewy (in a good way). Yummy.

The owner was extremely friendly and chatted with me and my friend and ended up bringing us an extra beer on the house!< /Text>

<Review>My only experience with Mongolian food is the BBQ on the round top grill. You get in a line and stuff frozen strips of meat into a bowl, then veggies, top with some sauce and then hand to a cook who uses two sticks on a round grill to cook up your own creation. While this was always a fun and tasty experience, it definitely felt pretty westernized.

Togi's is a traditional, sit down, restuarant. They have an off Japanese restaurant type of feel, which includes bar/counter seating that looks oddly like a sushi restaurant. Maybe remnants from a prior proprietor? No matter, the food is unique and tasty.

I tried the first dish on the menu, which after ordering looks to be what every table in the place also ordered. It was called Tsuvian and was a noodle dish that came with stir fried meat and veggies mixed into the noodles and served on a hot cast iron plate. The flavor was not heavily spiced, but did not lack flavor. The noodles were delicious and highlighted the natural flavor of the meat and veggies.

The experience here left me curious about other dishes that are unique to Mongolian cuisine. I will likely be back here soon to try more!< /Review>< username>
Neville</username>

<username>Paula Ogden</username><date>1521582523709< /date><Rating>5<//Rating><text>I have lived at the Marina Village West Apartments TWICE in the last ten years.  First in a two bedroom with patio, which was very comfortable and well maintained.  I moved when I purchased a house and I never had a bit of problem receiving my deposits or negotiating any of my paperwork.  Marianne is terrific and so is her staff, but you have to be responsible for your own communication.  Seriously, as a tenant, I never had a problem with maintenance or anything else, so long as I communicated my needs to the office (respectfully) and gave them enough time to correct my concerns.  When I look at some of these other reviews I believe that some reviewers lose sight of the fact that as a tenant, you become responsible for creating the kinds of relationships you are going to have in this kind of living environment; you have neighbors; you are a neighbor, so be a good one.  As far as the front office, I can't imagine a more professional or caring staff available to you, the tenant.

I moved there a second time recently due to a house fire.  This time Marianne agreed to a short term lease for six months until my home was repaired.  Wow!  How accommodating is that?!!  Believe me, she could have gotten a longer lease in today's market, but as a previous tenant she considered my needs as a person.  Again, when I moved back home this November, I had no issue with deposits or cleaning.  Beyond being a respectful and obliging property manager, Marianne is a decent and considerate human being.  She does take the time to treat you like a person, as does her staff.

The apartments themselves are getting a little older, but are well maintained.  The grounds are immaculate and the TWO swimming pools and work out room are as clean and inviting as the landscapes.  You don't have to apartment shop for long to see what's available in Stockton.  I have referred two friends who have enjoyed living at Marina Village West as well.  I have to laugh; a lot of people have lived in these apartments at one time or another.  It is most likely due to their ideal location.  They are just far enough away from the freeway and close to shopping and the 24 Hour Fitness.

Well, that's all I've got.  Thanks to Marianne and her staff for their kindness during my last six month stay.  I appreciated every conversation, every cup of office coffee, and every fire insurance fax you sent for me.

1/1 point for good service
1/1 point for the good atmosphere
0/3 points for food

I personally ordered the loaded fries ( fries with random spots of cheese and burnt bacon). It should have cheese all over the fries with crispy bacon. However, the bacon was hard and looked like charcoal.
The spinach and artichoke dip was terrible and I have no idea how to fix that.
Chili burger which probably had the worst chili I‚Äôve ever had, it was over salted, minimal meat, and had this odd flavor I couldn't figure out. The main symptom here seems to be overzealous salt, a pinch is needed not a handful. Needless to say, I wouldn‚Äôt return. This is unfortunate because I did like the place itself but the food was awful.</text>

<date>1559967548386< /date>< Rating>

<Review>Happened to be in the south bay for some work stuff, and on my way back did the "ok Google, show me Indian restaurants on the way" and this was one of the first options. And I'm like - huh, a dosa place that I haven't seen before?!
Anyways, dropped in. It's inside a strip mall, and so the space is VERY limited. There was a group of 4, who were waiting before me. I was alone, so I didn't have to wait for a seat.
You order at the counter. The prices are pretty good. I got the Madras coffee for $2.49, and the Madras or Bombay, I forget, masala dosa, for $9.99.
The dosa was yummy! And filling! Took longer than I would expect, but came out super hot. It was hard for me to break pieces off of it for a good two minutes. The lady at the counter said it'll be spicy, but it really wasn't. Though, like I said, yummy dosa - might be a little better than Madras Cafe even! The coffee was really good too. And very hot.

Now my gripes with the place.
Service is either bad, or non existent. I saw 3 people who work there overall, including the lady at the counter. She was pretty friendly, and good at explaining menu items if you're new to dosas (I saw a couple of people who came in after me, who most probably had never had dosa before).
The second guy was mostly cleaning tables, so I didn't really interact with him.
The third guy was very not friendly at all. Not particularly rude, but has this forever frown -y face.

Also, things move pretty slow in there. I asked for my coffee as soon as the dosa came out, and either they forgot or they're just slow, but it took another 5+ minutes before the coffee came out.
Similarly, I asked for a little extra coconut chutney (which, Madras Cafe makes better, BTW), when the little bit they gave, ran out, and it took a while for that to come out. Also, it was generally pretty hard to get someone's attention.

I still give it 4 stars because of the food. And the service part is something they should be able to fix easily. Give it a shot, but if you prefer faster, better service, and very similar food, go to Madras Cafe.</Review><Pictures>None< /Pictures><Response>None<//Response><Gmap_id>0x808fbbd999b82e1f:0x56b4eb63706a8a8</Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>
